Classificado por Maurice Nadeau como «o romance» da Resistência, foi traduzido para 27 línguas.\n\nEducação europeia narra a história de um jovem adolescente lituano polaco de 14 anos, Janek Twardowski, que vive refugiado na floresta e se junta a um grupo partisan para sobreviver e lutar contra a ocupação nazi.\n\nNeste conto moral, cruel e otimista, Janek conhecerá o frio, a fome, a traição e a morte, mas também o amor, junto da sua jovem amiga Zosia. Como diz o chefe partisan Dobranski, «a Europa teve sempre as melhores e mais belas universidades (…), elas foram o berço da civilização (…) mas há também uma outra educação europeia, a que recebemos hoje: os pelotões de execução, a escravatura, a tortura, a violação - a destruição de tudo o que torna a vida bela. É a hora das trevas.»\n\nCom os seus camaradas de infortúnio, a sua simplicidade e generosidade, Janek aprenderá o valor da amizade e a crença no Homem.<\/span>\n  <a       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/10838.Ismail_Kadare">About Ismail Kadare</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/10838.Ismail_Kadare"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1474491253p3/10838.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/10838.Ismail_Kadare">Ismail Kadare
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
1,122
followers
</div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer18285686112287270198">Ismail Kadare (also spelled Kadaré) is an Albanian novelist and poet. He has been a leading literary figure in Albania since the 1960s. He focused on short stories until the publication of his first novel, <i>The General of the Dead Army</i>. In 1996 he became a lifetime member of the Academy of Moral and Political Sciences of France. In 1992, he was awarded the <b>Prix mondial Cino Del Duca</b>; in 2005, he wo</span>
  <span id="freeText18285686112287270198" style="display:none">Ismail Kadare (also spelled Kadaré) is an Albanian novelist and poet. He has been a leading literary figure in Albania since the 1960s. He focused on short stories until the publication of his first novel, <i>The General of the Dead Army</i>. In 1996 he became a lifetime member of the Academy of Moral and Political Sciences of France. In 1992, he was awarded the <b>Prix mondial Cino Del Duca</b>; in 2005, he won the inaugural <b>Man Booker International Prize</b>, in 2009 the <b>Prince of Asturias Award of Arts</b>, and in 2015 the <b>Jerusalem Prize</b>. He has divided his time between Albania and France since 1990. Kadare has been mentioned as a possible recipient for the <b>Nobel Prize</b> in Literature several times. His works have been published in about 30 languages.<br /><br />Ismail Kadare was born in 1936 in Gjirokastër, in the south of Albania. His education included studies at the University of Tirana and then the Gorky Institute for World Literature in Moscow, a training school for writers and critics.<br /><br />In 1960 Kadare returned to Albania after the country broke ties with the Soviet Union, and he became a journalist and published his first poems.<br /><br />His first novel, <i>The General of the Dead Army</i>, sprang from a short story, and its success established his name in Albania and enabled Kadare to become a full-time writer. <br /><br />Kadare's novels draw on Balkan history and legends. They are obliquely ironic as a result of trying to withstand political scrutiny. Among his best known books are <i>Chronicle in Stone</i> (1977), <i>Broken April</i> (1978), and <i>The Concert</i> (1988), considered the best novel of the year 1991 by the French literary magazine <i>Lire</i>.<br /><br />In 1990, Kadare claimed political asylum in France, issuing statements in favour of democratisation. During the ordeal, he stated that "dictatorship and authentic literature are incompatible. The writer is the natural enemy of dictatorship."<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="18285686112287270198" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
